📚 DDCET 2026 — English & Computer
🗣
E1 = Comprehension — Unseen passage ma answer PASSAGE MA THI j aavse, apni knowledge thi nahi! Reading strategy: first skim karo → questions vaacho → phir detail ma vaacho. Time management important chhe — 10-12 mins max.
English · Chapter 01 · 10%

Comprehension of Unseen Passage

An unseen passage is given followed by 5 questions. You must read carefully and answer from the passage only.

Reading Strategy Types of Questions Finding Main Idea Inference Questions Vocabulary in Context
1.1

What is an Unseen Passage?

Unseen Passage: A reading passage that you have NOT studied before the exam. You read it during the exam and answer questions based only on what the passage says.Unseen passage ma answer PASSAGE MA THI j aape — apni general knowledge thi nahi. Passage dhyan thi vaacho! Your own general knowledge is secondary — the answer must be from the passage.

In DDCET, you get 1 passage followed by 5 MCQ questions. The passage is usually 150–300 words about a general topic (nature, science, communication, society, etc.).

1.2

Step-by-Step Reading Strategy

  1. Read the questions first (30 seconds) — Before reading the passage, skim the 5 questions. This tells you what to look for.
  2. Read the passage once fully — Don't stop at difficult words. Get the overall meaning and topic.
  3. Read again and underline key information — Focus on names, dates, causes, effects, and definitions.
  4. Answer each question — Go back to the passage to find the answer. Do NOT answer from memory or general knowledge.
  5. Check your answers — Verify each answer against the passage text.
1.3

Types of Questions and How to Answer

Question TypeHow to IdentifyStrategy
Factual / Direct"According to the passage…", "What does the passage say about…"Find the exact sentence in the passage with the answer. The answer is directly stated.
Main Idea / Title"What is the best title for this passage?", "The passage is mainly about…"The main idea covers the WHOLE passage, not just one part. Ask: what is the author's central point?
Inference / Implied"We can conclude that…", "It can be inferred that…", "The author suggests…"The answer is not directly stated but implied. Use clues from the text to reason.
Vocabulary in Context"The word '___' in the passage means…"Read the sentence around the word. Choose the meaning that fits best in that context.
True / False / Not Given"Which of the following is true/false according to the passage?"Check each option against the passage carefully. "Not Given" means the passage doesn't mention it.
1.4

Tips for Scoring Full Marks

  • Never guess without reading — All answers are in the passage.
  • Beware of "close but wrong" options — Examiners include options that sound correct but have one wrong word.
  • For vocabulary questions — The correct answer is a synonym that makes sense in that exact sentence.
  • For main idea questions — Avoid options that are too specific (only one paragraph) or too broad (beyond the passage).
  • Stay focused on the passage — Even if you know more about the topic, only what the passage says counts.
  • Avoid extreme options — Options with words like "always", "never", "all", "none" are usually wrong unless the passage clearly states so.
Practice Tip: Read one newspaper article or short story every day. This trains your brain to quickly understand passages and find key information.
1.5

Sample Passage + Questions

Sample Passage

"Communication is a fundamental human need. It allows people to share thoughts, express feelings, and coordinate actions. Humans communicate not only through words but also through gestures, facial expressions, and body language. Even silence can be a form of communication. When we listen carefully to another person, we show respect and build stronger relationships. Good communication skills are essential for success in both personal and professional life."

Q1. What is the passage mainly about?
→ (A) The importance of communication — ✓ CORRECT (covers whole passage)

Q2. According to the passage, how do humans communicate?
→ (D) Through words, gestures, facial expressions, body language, and silence — ✓ CORRECT

Q3. The word 'fundamental' in the passage most likely means:
→ (B) Basic and essential — ✓ CORRECT (context: "fundamental human need")

Q4. Which of the following can be inferred from the passage?
→ (C) Listening is as important as speaking — ✓ CORRECT (implied by "listen carefully = show respect")

Q5. The passage suggests good communication is important for:
→ (D) Both personal and professional life — ✓ CORRECT (last sentence)
🗣
E2 = Communication — Sender → Message → Channel → Receiver → Feedback. Verbal (words), Non-verbal (body language, gestures). Barriers: noise, language, cultural differences. Formal vs Informal communication — difference yaad karo!
English · Chapter 02 · 10%

Theory of Communication

Understanding how communication works, its types, and what blocks it. This chapter is directly tested with MCQs and fill-in-the-blanks.

Process of Communication Verbal Communication Non-Verbal Communication Barriers to Communication
2.1

What is Communication?

Communication: A branch of knowledge dealing with the principles and methods by which information is conveyed. It is the process of transferring information from the sender to the recipient.
Communication is an integral instinct present in all living beings. Every organism — humans, animals, plants — communicates in some way.

Why Do We Communicate?

  • To express our feelings, thoughts, and desires
  • To pass on information to others
  • To share knowledge and ideas
  • Communication is a dreadful need of survival — without it, we cannot express our desires.
If you have no power of communication, you cannot express your desire — this is the most important loss.

Communication in Nature

EntityHow they communicate
PlantsThrough visible changes in the colour of leaves, and the falling of leaves and flowers
AnimalsBy sounds and several movements — to indicate they are hungry, unwell, or need medical attention
Very young childrenBy crying
Parents showing angerBy not speaking for some times (silent treatment)
2.2

Process of Communication

Communication Process

Key Elements of Communication

ElementDefinition
SenderPerson who initiates the message; encodes the idea
MessageThe idea, information or emotion being transmitted
Channel / MediumThe method used — spoken word, letter, email, gesture, phone, etc.
Recipient / ReceiverPerson who receives and decodes the message
FeedbackThe receiver's response to the message — confirms whether communication was successful
Noise / BarrierAnything that interferes with the message being understood correctly
2.3

Types of Communication: Verbal vs Non-Verbal

Verbal Communication

  • Uses words — spoken or written
  • Oral: face-to-face conversation, phone calls, speeches, lectures
  • Written: letters, emails, reports, text messages
  • Precise and can be documented
  • Example: "Please come at 10 AM"

Non-Verbal Communication

  • Does NOT use words — uses body language, signals
  • Gesture: raising eyebrow, waving to a friend, nodding
  • Facial expression: smile, frown, surprise
  • Body language: posture, eye contact, distance
  • Often more powerful than words — conveys emotion instantly
A gesture like raising an eyebrow or waving to a friend can be used as a means to communicate — this is a key fact in DDCET questions.
2.4

Barriers to Communication

Barriers: Factors that block or interfere with the message that someone is trying to send, preventing effective communication.
Type of BarrierExamples & Explanation
Physical BarriersDistance, noise, poor lighting, faulty equipment
Language BarriersUsing unfamiliar technical terms or over-complicated language that cannot be understood well. Also: difference in dialects of different regions, unfamiliar accents.
Physiological BarriersIf the receiver has hearing problems, or the speaker has speech disabilities, then communication will not be effective.
Psychological BarriersStress, emotions, prejudice, lack of interest — distort how message is sent or received
Cultural BarriersDifferent customs, values, and assumptions between sender and receiver
Semantic BarriersSame word meaning different things to different people; jargon; ambiguous language

Key DDCET Facts on Barriers

  • Unfamiliar accents can make it difficult to understand the message sent.
  • The difference in dialects of different regions can also be a barrier.
  • Barriers block or interfere with the message that someone is trying to send.
  • If the receiver has hearing problems → communication will not be effective.
  • Using unfamiliar terms or over-complicated technical terms → message cannot be understood well.

How to Overcome Barriers

  • Use simple, clear language
  • Give and seek feedback
  • Be a good listener — active listening
  • Choose appropriate channel for the message
  • Be aware of cultural differences
  • Minimize physical distractions and noise
Chapter 2 — MCQ Answer Key
MCQ na answers verify karo — same pattern ni questions exam ma aave chhe!
  • Without communication → cannot express our desire
  • Plants communicate → changes in colour of leaves, falling of leaves and flowers
  • Animals communicate → by sound and several movements (to indicate hungry/unwell)
  • Children communicate anger → by crying | Parents anger → by not speaking
  • Communication is a dreadful need of survival
  • Barriers block → the message that someone is trying to send
  • Hearing problems → communication will not be effective
  • Unfamiliar accents → can make it difficult to understand the message
  • A gesture (raising eyebrow, waving) → means of communication

E3 = Letter Writing — Formal letter: receiver address, date, subject, body, yours faithfully/sincerely. Email: To, CC, Subject, Salutation, Body, Signature. Complaint letter ane Inquiry letter format alag alag chhe — dono yaad karo!
English · Chapter 03 · 10%

Techniques of Writing

Business letters, email writing, formal formats and abbreviations — the practical tools of professional written communication.

Parts of a Letter Parts of an Email Inquiry Letter Complaint Letter Order Letter Common Abbreviations
3.1

Parts of a Business Letter

A formal business letter has 8 standard parts, written in a specific order.

#PartWhat it ContainsExample
1Sender's AddressYour address (NOT your name)12, MG Road, Surat – 395001
2DateDate the letter is written13th April 2026 or 13/04/2026
3Receiver's Address (Inside Address)Name and address of the person you're writing toThe Manager, XYZ Ltd., Ahmedabad
4SubjectBrief statement of the letter's purpose (1 line)Subject: Inquiry regarding product prices
5SalutationFormal greetingDear Sir/Madam, To Whom It May Concern,
6BodyMain content — Opening, Middle (main message), Closing (action required)3 short paragraphs
7Complimentary CloseFormal goodbyeYours faithfully, / Yours sincerely,
8SignatureYour name, designationRamesh Patel, Manager
Use Yours faithfully when salutation is "Dear Sir/Madam" (you don't know the name). Use Yours sincerely when salutation uses the person's name (Dear Mr. Patel).
3.2

Parts of an Email

PartDescription
To:Email address of the primary recipient
CC:Carbon Copy — others who receive a copy of the email (they can see each other)
BCC:Blind Carbon Copy — hidden recipients (others cannot see BCC recipients)
Subject:Brief, clear title of the email's purpose
SalutationDear Sir/Madam, Dear [Name],
BodyOpening → Main message → Closing request
ClosingRegards, / Best regards, / Yours sincerely,
SignatureFull name, designation, contact, company name
AttachmentFiles attached to the email (indicated with 📎)
3.3

Types of Business Letters

1. Inquiry Letter

Purpose: To ask for information about products, services, prices, availability, or terms.
Key phrases: "We would like to inquire about…", "Please provide us with details regarding…", "Kindly send us your latest catalogue and price list…"

2. Reply to Inquiry Letter

Purpose: To respond to an inquiry with the requested information.
Key phrases: "Thank you for your inquiry dated…", "We are pleased to inform you that…", "Please find enclosed our catalogue/price list…"

3. Order Letter

Purpose: To officially place an order for goods or services. Should include quantity, product name, price, delivery terms, and payment method.
Key phrases: "Please supply us with the following…", "Please arrange delivery to our address by…", "Payment will be made by DD/NEFT within 30 days."

4. Complaint Letter

Purpose: To formally express dissatisfaction about a product, service, or situation and request a remedy.
Key phrases: "We regret to inform you that…", "The goods received were damaged/wrong/incomplete…", "We request you to replace/refund/rectify…", "We expect a prompt response."

5. Adjustment Letter

Purpose: Written in response to a complaint letter. It accepts the complaint and offers a solution (replacement, refund, apology).
Key phrases: "We sincerely apologize for the inconvenience caused…", "We are taking immediate steps to rectify…", "A replacement will be dispatched within 3 working days."
3.4

AbbreviationFull FormUse
Attn.AttentionDirecting letter to a specific person

BCCBlind Carbon CopyHidden copy recipients
Enc. / Encl.EnclosureDocuments attached with the letter
Ref.ReferenceReferring to a previous letter/document
Re.RegardingSubject of the letter
P.S.Post ScriptAdditional note after signature
P.T.O.Please Turn OverLetter continues on next page
E.O.D.End of DayDeadline — by end of working day

e.g.For example (Latin: exempli gratia)Giving examples
etc.And so on (Latin: et cetera)Continuing a list
vs. / v/sVersusComparing two things
approx.ApproximatelyAbout, roughly
dept.DepartmentSection of a company
mgr.ManagerTitle
pp.PagesReferring to multiple pages
no.NumberQuantity
qty.QuantityAmount/number of items
amt.AmountMonetary value
a.m. / p.m.Ante Meridiem / Post MeridiemBefore/after noon

FYIFor Your InformationSharing information informally

E4 = Grammar — DDCET ma most questions aa section thi aave chhe! Tenses (12 types), Active/Passive voice, Direct/Indirect speech, Subject-verb agreement, Articles (a, an, the). Rules clear karva → practice sentences solve karo!
English · Chapter 04 · 10%

Grammar

Parts of speech, tenses, and subject-verb agreement — the core grammatical rules you need to know for DDCET.

Parts of Speech Nouns Pronouns Adjective & Adverb Verb Preposition Tenses Subject-Verb Agreement
4.1

Parts of Speech

Every word in English belongs to one of 8 Parts of Speech based on its function in a sentence.

#Part of SpeechDefinitionExamples
1NounName of a person, place, thing, idea, or qualityRahul, Surat, book, honesty, team
2PronounReplaces a noun to avoid repetitionI, he, she, it, they, we, who, which, this
3AdjectiveDescribes or modifies a noun or pronounbig, blue, happy, three, best
4AdverbModifies a verb, adjective, or another adverb — tells how, when, where, how muchquickly, yesterday, here, very, too
5VerbShows an action, occurrence, or state of beingrun, is, has, went, seems, play
6PrepositionShows relationship between a noun/pronoun and another word (position, time, direction)in, on, at, by, for, with, under, above, between
7Conjunction / ConnectorJoins words, phrases, or clausesand, but, or, because, although, however, therefore
8InterjectionExpress sudden feeling or emotion; grammatically independentOh! Wow! Ouch! Hey! Alas!

Nouns — Types

TypeDefinitionExamples
Proper NounSpecific name of a person, place, or thing — always capitalisedRahul, Mumbai, Monday, Tata
Common NounGeneral name of a class of persons, places, or thingsboy, city, company, day
Collective NounName of a group of persons, animals, or thingsteam, flock, class, jury, committee
Abstract NounName of quality, state, action, or idea — cannot be touched or seenhonesty, happiness, justice, knowledge
Material NounName of a material or substancegold, water, wood, iron

Pronouns — Types

TypeExamplesUse
PersonalI, you, he, she, it, we, they, me, him, her, us, themRefer to persons or things
Possessivemy, your, his, her, its, our, their, mine, yours, his, hersShow ownership
Reflexivemyself, yourself, himself, herself, itself, ourselves, themselvesWhen subject and object are same person
Relativewho, whom, whose, which, thatConnect clauses; refer to nouns just mentioned
Demonstrativethis, that, these, thosePoint to specific nouns
Interrogativewho, what, which, whose, whomAsk questions
Common mistake: "Me and my brother decided..." → WRONG. Correct: "My brother and I decided..." — Use subject pronouns (I, he, she, we, they) as subject of verb.Yaad rakho: "Me and my brother" GALAT chhe — "My brother and I" SACHU chhe. Subject ma "I" j vaparay!
4.2

Tenses

Tenses show when an action takes place. There are 3 main tenses × 4 aspects = 12 tenses in English.

TenseStructureExample
Simple PresentSubject + V1 (s/es for he/she/it)She reads every day.
Present Continuousam/is/are + V-ingShe is reading now.
Present Perfecthas/have + V3 (past participle)She has read the book.
Present Perfect Continuoushas/have been + V-ingShe has been reading for 2 hours.
Simple PastSubject + V2 (past form)She read the book yesterday.
Past Continuouswas/were + V-ingShe was reading when I called.
Past Perfecthad + V3She had read the book before the exam.
Past Perfect Continuoushad been + V-ingShe had been reading for 2 hours when I arrived.
Simple Futurewill/shall + V1She will read tomorrow.
Future Continuouswill be + V-ingShe will be reading at 8 PM.
Future Perfectwill have + V3She will have read by then.
Future Perfect Continuouswill have been + V-ingShe will have been reading for 3 hours.
Signal words: Present perfect → "since, for, already, just, yet, ever, never". Past perfect → "before, after, by the time, already, when". Simple past → "yesterday, last week, ago, in 1990".
4.3

Subject-Verb Agreement

The verb must agree with its subject in number (singular/plural) and person (1st/2nd/3rd).

RuleCorrectWrong
Singular subject → singular verb (add s/es)He reads books.He read books. ✗
Plural subject → plural verb (no s/es)They read books.They reads books. ✗
I and You take plural verbI write. You write.I writes. ✗
Two subjects joined by 'and' → pluralRam and Shyam are here.Ram and Shyam is here. ✗
Either/Neither/Each/Every/None → singularEach student has a book.Each student have ✗
Collective nouns (team, class, jury) → singular in IndiaThe team has won.The team have won. ✗
Subject joined by "or/nor" → verb agrees with nearest subjectNeither he nor they are ready.Neither he nor they is ready. ✗
Indefinite pronouns (everyone, nobody, someone) → singularEveryone needs food.Everyone need food. ✗
4.4

Prepositions

PrepositionUseExamples
inInside a space; months, years, seasonsin the room, in January, in 2026
onSurface; days; specific dateson the table, on Monday, on 5th April
atSpecific time; specific placeat 9 AM, at the station
forDuration of time; purposefor two hours, for my health
sinceFrom a specific point in time (used with perfect tenses)since Monday, since 2020
byDeadline; beside; agent in passiveby Friday, by the river, written by Tagore
betweenAmong two thingsbetween 5 and 7 PM, between you and me
amongAmong three or moreamong the students
4.5

Verb Types — All 9 Types

Verbs are the backbone of every sentence. DDCET asks you to identify verb types from underlined words.

TypeDefinitionExample
Transitive VerbAction verb that needs an object to complete its meaningShe ate the cake. (object = cake) | "Would you take a picture for us?"
Intransitive VerbAction verb that does NOT need an object; sense is complete"The mail arrived after I left." — arrived has no object
Helping / Auxiliary VerbSupports the main verb; does not carry main meaning"The grocery clerk will carry your bags." — 'will' = helping verb
Main VerbThe principal verb that carries the main meaning"Jerry studies for three hours every day." — 'studies' = main verb
Regular VerbForms past tense by adding -ed / -dwalk → walked, play → played, love → loved
Irregular VerbPast tense does NOT follow -ed pattern; changes formgo → went, do → done, look → looked? No — look → looked (regular). See → saw, bring → brought
Dynamic / Action VerbDescribes an action that can be performed (physically or mentally)"I don't want to fight about who gets the car." — fight = dynamic/action
Stative VerbDescribes a state, NOT an action; usually not used in continuous form"I prefer cream rather than milk." — prefer = stative (know, love, hate, seem, believe)
Linking VerbConnects subject to a description (complement), not an action"That book you recommended sounds interesting." — sounds links subject to 'interesting'

SentenceUnderlined WordAnswer

Common Auxiliary / Helping Verbs

Primary: be (is/am/are/was/were), have (has/had), do (does/did)
Modal: can, could, will, would, shall, should, may, might, must, need, dare, ought to
📌 Key Rule — Stative Verbs NOT used in Continuous (-ing) Form
Do NOT say: "I am knowing the answer" ✗ — Say: "I know the answer" ✓
Stative verbs: know, believe, understand, love, hate, prefer, want, need, seem, appear, contain, belong, own, have (possession) Stative verbs = state dikhave, action nahi — aa verbs ne "-ing" form ma vaaparvana nahi (exam trap!)
4.6

Adjective Types — Quality, Quantity, Number

An adjective modifies a noun. In DDCET, you must identify WHICH TYPE of adjective a word is.

TypeWhat it tellsExamplesKey Words
Adjective of Quality
(Descriptive)		Describes the quality or characteristic of a nounbig, wise, ferocious, foolish, honest, beautiful, tall, heavy, goodAnswers: "What kind of?"
Adjective of Quantity
(Quantitative)		Refers to approximate amount/quantity (NOT exact number)some, little, much, all, sufficient, no, enough, a lot of, a little, a fewAnswers: "How much?"
Adjective of Number
(Numeral)		Refers to the number or order of nounsfive, several, many, first, every, each, both, second, few (countable)Answers: "How many?" or "In what order?"

Exercise 4A — Key Answers from DDCET PDF

SentenceAdjectiveType

The foolish crow opened his mouth to sing.foolishQuality
He has little patience.littleQuantity
He has lost all of his wealth.allQuantity
We did not receive sufficient rain this year.sufficientQuantity
Each hand has five fingers.fiveNumber
There are several mistakes in your composition.severalNumber
January is the first month of the year.firstNumber
Our country expects every citizen to do their duty.everyNumber (Distributive)
Quick Trick: Quality → "What kind?" | Quantity → "How much?" (approximate, uncountable) | Number → "How many?" (exact or order)
4.7

Adverb Types — 5 Types

An adverb modifies a verb, adjective, or another adverb. In DDCET you must identify the adverb AND its type.

TypeAnswers the QuestionExamples
Adverb of MannerHow? In what way?slowly, quickly, loudly, sweetly, merrily, gracefully, lazily, diligently, patiently, easily
Adverb of PlaceWhere? In what direction?here, there, everywhere, outside, inside, above, below, up, down, near, away
Adverb of TimeWhen? For how long?now, today, yesterday, soon, already, lately, then, early, today
Adverb of FrequencyHow often?always, often, usually, seldom, never, sometimes, occasionally, frequently
Adverb of DegreeHow much? To what extent?very, quite, extremely, highly, almost, too, nearly, a bit, a little, pretty, enough

Example: "I am ........ tired" → (very); "It is ........ confusing" → (extremely); paintings at Ajintha are "........ beautiful" → (very)
4.8

Connectors / Conjunctions — All Types

Connectors join words, phrases, or clauses. DDCET asks you to fill in the correct connector between two sentences.

ConnectorType / UseExample
andAddition — adds two ideas togetherAditi is a good dancer. Madri is a good dancer. → Aditi and Madri are good dancers.
but / yet / stillContrast — opposite ideasAnila works diligently. She doesn't get promotion. → Anila works diligently but she doesn't get promotion.
or / otherwiseAlternative — choice / warningBe regular in class. You will not understand the subject. → Be regular in class, or you will not understand the subject.
so / thereforeResult / ConsequenceThe machine is out of order. Production is delayed. → The machine is out of order, so production is delayed.
because / since / for / asReason / CauseI always remember Prof. Munshi because he inspired me a lot.
though / although / even thoughConcession — despite the factThe teacher tried nicely. Students couldn't understand it. → Although the teacher tried nicely, students couldn't understand it.
however / asContrast (formal)He is hardworking. However, he doesn't get appreciation.
in spite of / despiteConcession (with noun/gerund)The teacher tried nicely. Students couldn't understand. → In spite of trying nicely, students couldn't understand.
if / unlessConditionYou work sincerely. You will get promotion. → If you work sincerely, you will get promotion.
either…or / neither…norCorrelative — pairsEither he goes, or I go.
not only…but also / both…andCorrelative — addition emphasisEnglish is useful. Both useful and important.
who / whom / whoseRelative — for personsThe Geetanjali was written by Tagore who was a great poet and painter.
which / thatRelative — for thingsThe radio which my father bought from Japan is here.
when / where / whyAdverbial — time, place, reasonThis is the palace where Shivaji was born.
till / until / before / after / sinceTime connectorsHe slept 9 am. Then he woke up. | Wait till your turn comes.
because of / due to / on account of / owing toReason (followed by noun/gerund)He failed due to carelessness.
Connector Quick Test: "He is hardworking. He doesn't get appreciation." — What connector? Use 'but' (contrast) or 'however' (formal contrast). "She is ill. She came to work." → Despite being ill, she came to work. / She came to work even though she was ill.

Connectors — Fill in the Blank: Key Exam Questions

Sentences to JoinCorrect Connector
Our teacher is kind. __ I like him.so (result)
She is weak. __ she walks fast.but (contrast)
Naresh got good marks. __ he was dull.though (concession)
The doctor came. __ the patient had died.but or while
We shall get good crops. __ it rains much.if (condition)
I feel happy. India has won. (reason)because
Attend classes regularly. __ you will get good result.unless (negative condition)
It is late. He will not be punished.but
Do not go out. It is raining.because
4.9

Prepositions — All Types and Exercises

in / on / at — Basic Rules

PrepositionUse for PLACEUse for TIME
inInside an enclosed space: in the room, in the boxMonths, years, seasons, long periods: in June, in 1996, in the morning
onOn a surface: on the table, on the wall, on the floorDays, dates: on Monday, on 15th June, on Holi
atSpecific point: at the bus stop, at the airportSpecific time: at 9 AM, at noon, at the end of the day
Exercise 9 Key Answers: man in the tub | cup on the table | juice in the glass | green board on the wall | lamp on the table | Exercise 15: 15th June → on | June → in | 1996 → in | Sunday → on | 12.30 pm → at | morning → in | Holi → on | 11th century → in

out of / off / inside / outside

  • out of = from inside to outside (exiting): The passengers are out of the plane.
  • off = away from surface / detached: He jumped off the balcony.
  • inside = within / interior: Their luggage is inside.
  • outside = exterior / not inside: He came outside the house and locked the door.

Positional Prepositions

PrepositionMeaningExample
in front ofFacing / beforeThe lady is standing in front of the mirror.
behindAt the back ofThe girl is standing behind the door.
betweenIn the middle of twoThe bank and library are between the shopping mall.
amongIn the middle of many (3+)He distributed the prize among the three boys.
near / besideClose toAmit is sitting near/beside his mother.
up / downHigher / lower directionWe walked up the stairs.
from / to / towardsDirection/originGujarat is between Rajasthan and Madhya Pradesh. | Coming from home.

by / till / until / before / after / for / since / from / to

PrepositionUseExample
byNot later than (deadline)I will reach your home by 6 pm today.
till / untilUp to a time (duration)Wait till/until your turn comes.
beforeEarlier thanDo your work before the teacher came.
afterLater thanHe slept 9 am. Then he woke up and went out.
forDuration (how long)I have been waiting here for three hours.
sinceFrom a point in time (exact start)I have been waiting here since 5 o'clock.
from…toRange of time or placeI go to the class from 6 pm to 8 pm.

in / on / by — Transport Prepositions

by = mode of transport (general): travel by air, go by train, travel by foot
in = inside a vehicle: travel in a taxi, come in a car
on = open/public transport: go on foot, ride on a horse
Grammar Quick Rules
Grammar na rules fast yaad karva maate aa shortcuts use karo — exam ma time bachshe!
  • Subject pronoun (I/he/she/we/they) → used as subject | Object pronoun (me/him/her/us/them) → after verbs/prepositions
  • Myself, yourself etc. → only used when subject and object are same person
  • Present perfect: have/has + V3 (not "I have went" → WRONG; "I have gone" → correct)
  • Conditional: "If I had known… I would have gone" (NOT "would of" — that's WRONG)
  • their = possession | there = place | they're = they are
  • its = possession | it's = it is
  • your = possession | you're = you are

5.2

Common Grammatical Errors — From DDCET Papers

Their / There / They're

WordMeaningCorrect Example
TheirPossession (belonging to them)Their dog ran away while they were in the park. ✓
TherePlace / existsThere is a dog there. ✓
They'reThey are (contraction)They're going to the park. ✓

It's vs Its | You're vs Your | We're vs Were

ContractionPossessive
it's = it is → It's been three weeksits = belonging to it → The cat licked its paw
you're = you areyour = belonging to you
we're = we arewere = past tense of "be"

Sentence Correction — Practice Questions & Answers

1. Choose grammatically correct: "It's been three weeks since we last ___ him."
✓ CORRECT: "It's been three weeks since we last saw him."
Reason: Use simple past (saw) after "since" with present perfect (it's been).
2. Pick grammatically correct sentence about the dog
✓ CORRECT: "Their dog ran away while they were in the park."
Reason: "Their" = possession. "Were" = past of "be" (they were in the park).
3. Incorrect punctuation: coffee question
✓ INCORRECT: "Can you please pick me up a coffee, while you are out."
Reason: A question must end with (?) not a period (.). Should be: "Can you please pick me up a coffee while you are out?"
4. "He ____ the train to get to work." — Choose correct
✓ CORRECT: "He took the train to get to work."
Reason: Use simple past (took) for a habitual past action. "He takes" is also possible for present habit. "He take" ✗ (missing s). "He taking" ✗ (no auxiliary verb).
5. Grammatically incorrect sentence about "best"
✓ INCORRECT: "My car ran more better than hers."
Reason: "more better" is a double comparative — WRONG. Should be just "better".
6. "If I had known about the party, I would have ___"
✓ CORRECT: "If I had known about the party, I would have gone to it."
Reason: Conditional type 3 = "If + past perfect, would have + past participle". NEVER "would of" — that is wrong.
7. Apostrophe error: The cat's ran away
✓ INCORRECT: "The cat's ran away when the dog's arrived."
Reason: "cat's" and "dog's" are possessive forms — wrongly used here. Should be "cats ran away when the dogs arrived." (plural, no apostrophe needed for simple plural).
8. "Me and my brother" vs "My brother and I"
✓ INCORRECT: "Me and my brother decided to get our parents a gift."
✓ CORRECT: "My brother and I decided to get our parents a gift."
Reason: "I" is a subject pronoun. "Me" is an object pronoun — cannot be the subject of a verb.
9. Dangling modifier: "at eight years old"
✓ INCORRECT: "My father decided to give me a pony for Christmas, at eight years old."
Reason: The phrase "at eight years old" appears to modify "father" (making him eight years old) — but the intended meaning is that I was eight. This is a dangling modifier. Correct: "At eight years old, I received a pony from my father for Christmas."
5.2b

Find the INCORRECT Spelling — From DDCET PDF

In this type, 4 options are given and you must find the ONE that is spelled WRONG.

Q#Incorrect Spelling (WRONG)Correct Spelling
19ManeouvreManoeuvre
20StrenthStrength
21RunerRunner
22PlesantPleasant
23PreceedingPreceding
24NeccessaryNecessary (one 'c', two 's')
25InsistanceInsistence (ance → ence)
26AdvurtiseAdvertise
27LiesureLeisure (ei not ie after L)
28DiscribeDescribe
📌 Tricky Spelling Rules
i before e except after c: believe, achieve, receive (after c = ei), perceive
Exceptions: seize, leisure, weird, either, neither
-ance vs -ence: insistence, competence, convenience, dependence | assistance, tolerance, appearance
Double consonant: runner (run+n+er), occurrence (occur+r+ence), commitment (commit+t+ment)
Silent letters: Pneumonia (P silent), Playwright (silent gh)
Rule yaad karo: "I before E except after C" — receive, deceive, conceive (C pachhi EI aave). Baaki jagye IE j aave: believe, achieve, relief

5.3

Key Grammar Rules to Remember

RuleWrong ✗Correct ✓
Subject pronoun as subjectMe and John wentJohn and I went
Past perfect conditionalI would of goneI would have gone
Past tense of "bring"We bringedWe brought
Past tense of "go"I have wentI have gone
Double comparativemore betterbetter
Double negativeI don't have no petsI have no pets / I don't have any pets
Question formDo you doing?What do you do? / What are you doing?
Comma spliceRachel is smart she began reading earlyRachel is smart; she began reading early.
Colon for explanationHe thought it was great: his manager didn't agree (needs conjunction after colon)He thought it was great; however, his manager didn't agree.
Commas in listscat and bird to see the vet (no comma)She took her dog, cat, and bird to see the vet.

9.1

Computer Basics

Generations of Computers

GenerationYearTechnologyLanguageI/O
1st Generation1945–1958Vacuum Tubes and ValvesMachine languageAll types for output (punched card, magnetic tape, paper tape); magnetic drum for memory; used Decimal Numbering System
2nd Generation1959–1964TransistorsCOBOL (started in 2nd gen)Magnetic tape & disk
3rd Generation1965–1970Integrated Circuit (IC) — SSI/MSIFORTRAN II-IV, BASIC, PASCAL, ALGOLAll (keyboard, disk)
4th Generation1971+Microprocessor (VLSI — Very Large Scale Integration)C++, CHard disk, floppy, CD
5th GenerationPresentULSI (Ultra Large Scale Integration), AIC#, Java (both a&b)All — keyboard, touch, scanner, CD/DVD, hard disk
ENIAC used vacuum tube technology. ENIAC was created in 1945, designed by J.P. Eckert & J.W. Mauchy at University of Pennsylvania, USA. ENIAC used all types for output (punched card, magnetic tape, paper tape) and used more than 2000 kW of electric power. ENIAC used Decimal Numbering System. ENIAC used Magnetic Drum for memory storage.

Memory Units

UnitSize
1 BitSmallest unit — stores 0 or 1
1 Nibble4 bits
1 Byte8 bits
1 KB (Kilobyte)1024 Bytes
1 MB (Megabyte)1024 KB = 1,048,576 Bytes
1 GB (Gigabyte)1024 MB
1 TB (Terabyte)1024 GB = 1024 MB
1 PB (Petabyte)1024 TB (largest common unit)
Order (smallest to largest): Bit → Nibble → Byte → KB → MB → GB → TB → PB. For CPU speed: Hz → KHz → MHz → GHz → THz

Computer Components and Terminology

TermFull Form / Meaning
CPUCentral Processing Unit — brain of the computer; does all processing
ALUArithmetic Logical Unit — part of CPU for calculating and comparing
Control UnitPart of CPU that selects, interprets, and executes program instructions
RAMRandom Access Memory — primary, volatile memory (lost on power off)
ROMRead Only Memory — non-volatile; stores BIOS
BIOSBasic Input Output System — first program run on startup
CMOSComplementary Metal Oxide Semiconductor
ASCIIAmerican Standard Code for Information Interchange
DMADirect Memory Access
SRAMStatic Random Access Memory
DRAMDynamic Random Access Memory
USBUniversal Serial Bus
CPU cycleTime required for fetching and execution of one machine instruction
CMYKCyan, Magenta, Yellow & Black (color printing model)
UNIVACUniversal Automatic Computer (first commercial computer)
HMOSHigh Speed MOS technology (name applied by Intel Corp.)
EBCDIC8-bit code used in Mainframe Computers
RegisterA set of flip-flops integrated together; stores CPU data temporarily
Flip FlopCapable of storing a single binary bit (0 or 1)
InterfaceCommon boundary between two systems
Bit manipulationExamination and changing of single bits or small groups within a word
1 millisecond1/1000th of a second (1000th of a second)
HardwarePhysical components of a computer (consume electric power, occupy space)
SoftwarePrograms/instructions (does not occupy physical space)

Types of Computers

TypeDescription
Mainframe ComputerLargest computer; supports thousands of concurrent users. Uses EBCDIC 8-bit code.
Mini ComputerMid-range; supports 100–200 concurrent users. Mini-computer is also called workstation.
Micro Computer / Personal Computer (PC)Most common at homes & offices; also called micro-computer
Workstation ComputerFor professional CAD/CAM, animation, high-power gaming
ABCAtanasoff-Berry Computer — special purpose computer
ENIACElectronic Numerical Integrator and Computer — first general purpose

Input / Output / Storage Devices

Input Devices

  • Keyboard (Caps Lock toggles capital letters; Print Screen saves screenshot; Num Lock toggles number pad)
  • Mouse
  • Scanner (processes drawings/characters on paper)
  • Light pen
  • Digital tablet (converts handwriting to computer input)
  • Joystick, Trackball
  • O.M.R (Optical Mark Reader — reads pencil marks on paper)
  • Badge reader (reads info from plastic cards)
  • Digitizer (converts graphics/pictures to binary)
  • Web cam

Output Devices

  • Monitor (most common) — CRT, LCD, LED, TFT, Plasma (>32")
  • Printer — Laser (best quality graphics), Plotter (pictorial form), Dot matrix (impact type), Ink jet
  • Plotter (translates computer data into pictorial form on paper)

Storage Devices

  • Hard disk (maximum data storage; primary storage)
  • Floppy disk (3", 5.25", 8"; high density = 1.44 MB)
  • CD/DVD
  • Backing store (secondary/auxiliary storage)
Plotter = best quality graphics. Laser printer = second best. Dot matrix = impact type printer. Modem = performs signal conversion (modulation/demodulation).

Display Resolutions & Aspect Ratios

ResolutionAspect RatioName
800 × 6004:3—
1280 × 72016:9HD
768 × 576576p—
1920 × 108016:9Full HD
CRT monitors (old)4:3—
PPI = Pixels Per Inch (number of pixels per inch of monitor length). HD = High Definition. TFT = Thin Film Transistor. LCD = Liquid Crystal Display. LED = Light Emitting Diode.

Programming Languages

LanguageNotes
FORTRANMore suited to structured programs; used in 1st gen computers
COBOLData division language; started from 2nd gen; program structure has data division
PASCALStructured language; data division is third division
BASICBeginner's language; started 2nd gen
LOGODevised by Dr. Seymour Aubrey Papert
PROLOGUsed for artificial intelligence
Assembly LanguageLow-level language; uses Mnemonics (memory tricks); translated by Assembler
Machine LanguageFirst gen computer programming language; binary 0s and 1s
C++, Java, C#4th/5th generation languages
Compiler = converts entire program to machine language at once. Assembler = converts assembly language to machine language. Interpreter = converts line by line.
9.2

MS Word

Key Facts

  • MS Word = software for preparation of documents
  • MS Excel = spreadsheets | MS Access = databases | MS PowerPoint = presentations
  • Default extension: .docx (also .doc — both valid)
  • Template extension: .dotx
  • WYSIWYG = What You See What You Get
  • Spelling errors: highlighted by red underline
  • Grammar errors: highlighted by green underline
  • Thesaurus tool: for Synonyms and Antonyms
  • Mail Merge: creates customized correspondence targeting different recipients
  • Mailing list in Word: called Data source
  • Default alignment: Left
  • Default header/footer: printed on every page
  • Font not a font style: Superscript (Bold, Italic, Regular are font styles)
  • Portrait and Landscape are Page orientation
  • OFFICE VISTA is not a valid version of MS Office
  • Pressing F8 three times → selects a sentence

9.3

MS Excel

Key Facts

  • MS Excel = software for spreadsheets
  • Each file in MS Excel = workbook
  • A worksheet is a collection of workbook (Excel is a collection of worksheets)
  • By default, worksheets named: Sheet1, Sheet2, Sheet3...
  • Columns: named in alphabets (A, B, C...)
  • Rows: named in numbers (1, 2, 3...)
  • Intersection of row and column = Cell
  • All formulas begin with = (equals sign)
  • Absolute cell reference: $A$1
  • Default extension (no macros): .xlsx
  • Extension for Excel 2007 workbook: .xlsx
  • MS Excel based on: Windows software
  • Common type of data: General
  • Data in a spreadsheet organized by: Rows and columns
  • Latest version: 10,48,576 rows and 16,384 columns
  • 1 MB = 1024 KB
  • 1 TB = 1024 MB (wait — 1 TB = 1024 GB; 1 GB = 1024 MB)
  • Graph does NOT exist as a chart type in MS Excel (Scatter, Line, Doughnut, Bar, Pie exist — "Graph" is not a valid chart type name)
  • Data Series is NOT available in Chart Options inside Chart Wizard
  • Data label options in charts: Series Name, Category, Value
  • Workbook = collection of worksheets

Important Functions

FunctionPurposeSyntax
=TODAY()Returns today's date (date value for day according to system clock)=TODAY()
=NOW()Returns current time=NOW()
=SUM()Adds values in range=SUM(A1:A5)
=AND()Returns TRUE only if ALL conditions are true=AND(A1>0, B1>0)
=OR()Returns TRUE if even ONE condition is true=OR(A1>0, B1>0)
=ABS()Returns positive value regardless of sign=ABS(-5) → 5
=MOD()Returns remainder after division=MOD(10,3) → 1
=DIV()Remainder function per DDCET textbook MCQ (Q32) — textbook answer differs from standard Excel; standard Excel uses MOD()Textbook answer
=ISBLANK()Returns TRUE if cell is blank=ISBLANK(A1)
=ISEVEN()Returns TRUE if cell contains even number=ISEVEN(4) → TRUE
=ISODD()Returns TRUE if cell contains odd number=ISODD(3) → TRUE
=DATE()Takes year, month, date values and displays given date=DATE(2026,4,13)
=DAY()Takes a date value and returns the day of month=DAY(A1)
=DATEVALUE()Takes a date string and returns parsed date value=DATEVALUE("13/4/2026")
=WEEKDAY()Returns day of week for given date=WEEKDAY(A1)
=WORKDAY()Returns date after given number of working days=WORKDAY(A1,5)
=YEARFRAC()Returns fractional year between given dates=YEARFRAC(A1,B1)
=MINUTES()Returns minutes from a time value=MINUTE(A1)
=SECOND()Returns seconds from a time value=SECOND(A1)
=CONCATENATE()Joins text strings together=CONCATENATE(A1,B1)
=N()Returns number equivalent of text value=N(A1)
=NA()Returns #NA error number=NA()

MS PowerPoint

Key Facts

  • MS PowerPoint = tool for preparation of presentations
  • Command line to open: powerpnt
  • Extension of presentation: .PPT
  • Template extension: N/A (save as .pot)
  • Suitable for: all types — educational, business, strategic (military)
  • Views: Slide Show, Slide Sorter, Normal — Outline view is NOT a standard view... wait — Outline view IS a view, but the question asks which is NOT. According to PDF: "Outline view" is not a view? Let me re-check — PDF says NOT = Outline view. ✓
  • Speaker Notes option: Notes View
  • Shadow, text color, box color: Color schemes
  • Stop slide show: Press Esc button
  • Font for presentation: from Home → Font menu
  • Paragraph style: from Home → Paragraph menu
  • Drawing: from Home → Drawing menu
  • Slide Design task pane: shows slide design currently used
  • Handout Master: defined by Layout of handout
  • Motion path: A method of moving items on a slide
  • Default page orientation: Landscape
  • Objects on slide that hold text: Placeholders
  • Optimum presentation duration: 22 to 35 minutes
  • Sound files for PPT: .wav files and .mid files
  • Video recording: record in video to find mistakes
  • To make effective presentation: minimize text, maximize all of them (images, videos, graphs)
  • Slide Transition = effect when slides change in slide show view
  • Lines, curve, freeform, scribble = Types of custom motion paths
  • AutoContent Wizard has 5 steps between Start and Finish
  • Task Pane controls all main slide tasks

Web Design — HTML & CSS

HTML Fundamentals

TermFull Form / Meaning
HTMLHyper Text Markup Language
DHTMLDynamic Hyper Text Markup Language
W3CWorld Wide Web Consortium (defines web standards)
WWWWorld Wide Web (father: Tim Berners-Lee, HTML proposed 1990)

RGBRed-Green-Blue

HTML type: Markup Language (not programming, not scripting). Web browser reads HTML. Fundamental HTML block = HTML Tag. Tags not displayed on page are written in <HEAD> section. File starts with <!doctype html>. Default extension: .html

Essential HTML Tags

TagPurpose
<html>...</html>Root element; document starts and ends with this
<head>...</head>Contains meta information, title, CSS links
<body>...</body>Visible page content
<H1> to <H6>Headings: H1 = biggest, H6 = smallest
<p>Paragraph
<b> or <strong>Bold text
<i>Italic text
<u>Underline text
<br>Line break
<img src="...">Display image
<a href="...">Hyperlink
<ul><li>Unordered (bulleted) list
<ol><li>Ordered (numbered) list
<DL>Descriptive list starts here
<table><tr><td>Table → row → cell
<th>Table heading cell
<thead>Table headings group
<caption>Table caption
<form>Form — attributes: method, action
<marquee>Scrolling text (behaviour property: alternate, blur, scroll — NOT "slide")
<style>CSS definitions inside this tag
<bdo>Supports Non-English language (bidirectional text)
Biggest heading = <H1>. Apart from <b>, <strong> also makes text bold. Body background: <body bgcolor="yellow">. Bulleted list with numbers = <ol>. Background image: <body background="sun.gif">. HTML tag begins with <. HTML tag ends with >.

HTML Colour Codes

Hex CodeColour
#FF0000Red
#00FF00Green
#0000FFBlue
#000000Black
#FFFFFFWhite
Hex color ranges from 00 to FF for each colour (0-FF). Each colour (R, G, B) has 2 hex digits.

CSS Essentials

  • CSS = Cascading Style Sheet — controls the appearance of HTML elements
  • Latest version: CSS3. First official W3C recommendation: CSS Level 1
  • 3 ways to add CSS: (1) header section <style> tag, (2) separate file (.css), (3) inline as attribute
  • CSS tag has 3 components: Selector, Property, Value (called Declaration)
  • In CSS: h1 = Selector. font-size = Property. color:red = Declaration
  • Correct syntax: body { color: black }
  • Class selector: matches element based on its class attribute
  • font-family property: changes the face of a font
  • CSS screen media type: for use with color computer screens
  • background-image property sets a background image
  • CSS property for align attribute = text-align
  • CSS property for <center> = margin
  • CSS extension prefixes for WebKit: -webkit
  • Web font format: WOFF | TTF developed by Apple & Microsoft late 1980s | First CSS = EOT
  • HSL = Hue Saturation Lightness
  • SVG = Scalable Vector Graphics

Computer Practice — Critical Facts Summary
  • CPU = brain | ALU = calculating & comparing | Control Unit = interprets instructions
  • RAM+ROM = Primary Memory | Hard disk, Floppy = Secondary (backing store)
  • ENIAC: 1945, J.P.Eckert & Mauchy, Univ. of Pennsylvania, vacuum tubes, all types for output (punched card/magnetic tape/paper tape), >2000 kW, Decimal Numbering System, Magnetic Drum memory
  • 1st gen = vacuum tube | 2nd = transistor | 3rd = IC | 4th = VLSI/microprocessor | 5th = ULSI/AI
  • Nibble=4bits | Byte=8bits | KB=1024B | MB=1024KB | GB=1024MB | TB=1024GB | PB=largest
  • Word file = .docx | Excel = .xlsx | PPT = .ppt | Word template = .dotx
  • Spelling error = red underline | Grammar error = green underline in MS Word
  • HTML = Markup Language | CSS = Cascading Style Sheet | WWW father = Tim Berners-Lee (1990)
  • #FF0000=Red | #00FF00=Green | #0000FF=Blue | #000000=Black | #FFFFFF=White
  • Ctrl+Z=Undo | Ctrl+Y=Redo | Ctrl+B=Bold | Ctrl+I=Italic | Ctrl+F=Find | F2=Edit cell
